{'item 1. ': 'Business Company Background Apple Computer, Inc. ("Apple" the "Company") was incorporated under the laws the State California January , . The Company designs, manufactures and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music and audio books. The Company\' products and services include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the iPod digital music player, the Xserve server and Xserve RAID storage products, portfolio consumer and professional software applications, the Mac operating system, the online iTunes Music Store, portfolio peripherals that support and enhance the Macintosh and iPod product lines, and variety other service and support offerings. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers and value added resellers. addition, the Company sells variety third-party products that are compatible with the Company\' Macintosh and iPod product lines, including computer printers and printing supplies, storage devices, computer memory, digital video and still cameras, personal digital assistants, iPod accessories, and various other computing products and supplies through its online and retail stores. The Company\' fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Unless otherwise stated, all information presented this Form - based the Company\' fiscal calendar. The Company\' strategy also includes expanding its distribution network effectively reach more its targeted customers. Xsan, the Company\' enterprise-class Storage Area Network (SAN) file system, was introduced beta version April and expected available for general release the Fall . Xsan -bit cluster file system for Mac that enables organizations consolidate storage resources and provide multiple computers with concurrent file-level read write access shared volumes over Fibre Channel. Advanced features such metadata controller failover and Fibre Channel multipathing ensure high availability; file-level locking allows multiple systems read and write concurrently the same volume which ideal for complex workflows; bandwidth reservation provides for effective ingestion bandwidth-intensive data streams, such high resolution video; and flexible volume management results more efficient use storage resources. Since Xsan interoperable with ADIC\' StorNext File System, can used heterogeneous environments that include Windows, UNIX and Linux server operating system platforms. Executive Overview Apple designs, manufactures and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops and markets line portable digital music ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK027:[04PAL0 04PAL1620]DI1620A.; \',USER=\'DNICHOL\', =\'; -DEC- ; : \' players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music and audio books. The Company\' products and services include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the iPod digital music player, the Xserve server and Xserve RAID storage products, portfolio consumer and professional software applications, the Mac operating system, the online iTunes Music Store, portfolio peripherals that support and enhance the Macintosh and iPod product lines, and variety other service and support offerings. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers and value added resellers. addition, the Company sells variety third-party Macintosh compatible products, including computer printers and printing supplies, storage devices, computer memory, digital video and still cameras, personal digital assistants, and various other computing products and supplies through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business and government customers. further description the Company\' products may found Part , Item this document under the heading "Business." The Company\' business strategy leverages its unique ability, through the design and development its own operating system, hardware and many software applications and technologies, bring its customers around the world compelling new products and solutions with superior ease- -use, seamless integration and innovative industrial design. The Company participates several highly competitive markets, including personal computers with its Macintosh line computers, consumer electronics with its iPod line digital music players and distribution third-party digital music through its online iTunes Music Store. While the Company widely recognized innovator the personal computer market well leader the emerging market for distribution digital music, these are highly competitive markets that are subject aggressive pricing and increased competition. order remain competitive, the Company believes that increased investment research and development ( & ) necessary order maintain and extend its position the markets where competes. The Company\' & spending focused delivering timely updates and enhancements its existing line personal computers, displays, operating systems, software applications and portable music players; developing new digital lifestyle consumer and professional software applications; and investing new product areas such rack-mount servers, RAID storage systems, and wireless technologies. The Company utilizes variety direct and indirect distribution channels. The Company believes that sales its innovative and differentiated products are enhanced knowledgeable salespersons who can convey the value the hardware, software and peripheral integration, demonstrate the unique digital lifestyle solutions that are available only Macintosh computers, and demonstrate the seamless compatibility the Macintosh with the Windows platform and networks. The Company further believes that providing high-quality sales and after-sales support experience critical attracting and retaining customers. ensure high-quality buying experience for its products which service and education are emphasized, the Company has expanded and improved its distribution capabilities opening its own retail stores the . and internationally. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products ( ., hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition. The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped, and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end-user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Future market conditions and product transitions may require the Company increase customer incentive programs and incur incremental price protection obligations that could result additional reductions revenue the time such programs are offered. Additionally, certain customer incentive programs require management estimate the number customers who will actually redeem the incentive based historical experience and the specific terms and conditions particular incentive programs. greater than estimated proportion customers redeem such incentives, the Company would required record additional reductions revenue, which could have material adverse impact the Company\' results operations. Inventory Valuation and Inventory Purchase Commitments The Company must order components for its products and build inventory advance product shipments. The Company performs detailed review inventory each period that considers multiple factors including demand forecasts, product life cycle status, product development plans, current sales levels, and component cost trends. The personal computer industry subject rapid and unpredictable pace product and component obsolescence and demand changes. future demand market conditions for the Company\' products are less favorable than forecasted unforeseen technological changes negatively impact the utility component inventory, the Company may required record additional write-downs which would negatively affect gross margins the period when the write-downs are recorded. The Company accrues necessary reserves for cancellation fees related component orders that have been cancelled. Consistent with industry practice, the Company acquires components through combination formal purchase orders, supplier contracts, and open orders based projected demand information. These commitments typically cover the Company\' requirements for periods ranging from days. there abrupt and substantial decline demand for one more the Company\' products unanticipated change technological requirements for any the Company\' products, the Company may required record additional reserves for cancellation fees that would negatively affect gross margins the period when the cancellation fees are identified. Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation The Company currently measures compensation expense for its employee stock-based compensation plans using the intrinsic value method prescribed Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion . , Accounting for Stock Issued Employees and provides pro forma disclosures the effect net income and earnings per share the fair value-based method had been applied measuring compensation expense. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, further discussed Part , Item this Form - Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation , requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. March , , the FASB issued proposed Statement, Share-Based Payment, that addresses the accounting for share-based payment transactions which enterprise receives employee services exchange for ( ) equity instruments the enterprise ( ) liabilities that are based the fair value the enterprise\' equity instruments that may settled the issuance such equity instruments. The proposed Statement would eliminate the ability account for share-based compensation transactions using APB Opinion . and generally would require instead that such transactions accounted for using fair-value-based method. adopted, currently anticipated that the proposed Statement would effective for the Company beginning its fourth fiscal quarter . the Company\' annual shareholders meeting April , , shareholders approved proposal requesting that the Company\' Board Directors (the Board) establish policy expensing the value all future employee stock options issued the Company. The Board and management appreciate and take seriously the views expressed the Company\' shareholders. The Company decided not expense the value employee stock options until the FASB finalizes its new accounting standard the matter, which may play significant role determining the fair value and accounting for employee stock options. The Company monitors progress the FASB and other developments with respect the general issue employee stock compensation. The Company currently reviewing the potential impact from the guidance the proposed statement, which may require the Company recognize substantially more compensation expense future periods that could have material adverse impact the Company\' future results operations. The accounting impact had the Company chosen apply the fair-value recognition provisions SFAS . , instead the recognition provisions under APB Opinion . , described Part , Item this Form - Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements. Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures About Market Risk Interest Rate and Foreign Currency Risk Management The Company regularly reviews its foreign exchange forward and option positions and its interest rate swap and option positions, both stand-alone basis and conjunction with its underlying foreign currency and interest rate related exposures. However, given the effective horizons the Company\' risk management activities and the anticipatory nature the exposures, there can assurance the hedges will offset more than portion the financial impact resulting from movements either foreign exchange interest rates. addition, the timing the accounting for recognition gains and losses related mark- -market instruments for any given period may not coincide with the timing gains and losses related the underlying economic exposures and, therefore, may adversely affect the Company\' operating results and financial position. Interest Rate Risk While the Company exposed interest rate fluctuations many the world\' leading industrialized countries, the Company\' interest income and expense most sensitive fluctuations the general level . interest rates. this regard, changes . interest rates affect the interest earned the Company\' cash, cash equivalents, and short-term investments well costs associated with foreign currency hedges. The Company\' short-term investment policy and strategy ensure the preservation capital, meet liquidity requirements, and optimize return light current credit and interest rate trends. The Company benchmarks its performance utilizing external money managers manage small portion the aggregate investment portfolio. The external managers adhere the Company\' investment policies and also provide occasional research and market information that supplements internal research used make credit decisions the investment process. The Company\' exposure market risk for changes interest rates relates primarily the Company\' investment portfolio. The Company places its short-term investments highly liquid securities issued high credit quality issuers and, policy, limits the amount credit exposure any one issuer. The Company\' general policy limit the risk principal loss and ensure the safety invested funds limiting market and credit risk. All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less are classified cash equivalents; highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. Foreign Currency Risk general, the Company net receiver currencies other than the . dollar. Accordingly, changes exchange rates, and particular strengthening the . dollar, may negatively affect the Company\' net sales and gross margins expressed . dollars. There also risk that the Company will have adjust local currency product pricing due competitive pressures when there has been significant volatility foreign currency exchange rates. The Company may enter into foreign currency forward and option contracts with financial institutions protect against foreign exchange risks associated with existing assets and liabilities, certain firmly committed transactions, forecasted future cash flows, and net investments foreign subsidiaries. Generally, the Company\' practice hedge majority its existing material foreign exchange transaction exposures. However, the Company may not hedge certain foreign exchange transaction exposures due immateriality, prohibitive economic cost hedging particular exposures, and limited availability appropriate hedging instruments. order provide meaningful assessment the foreign currency risk associated with certain the Company\' foreign currency derivative positions, the Company performed sensitivity analysis using value- -risk (VAR) model assess the potential impact fluctuations exchange rates. The VAR model consisted using Monte Carlo simulation generate random market price paths. The VAR the maximum expected loss fair value, for given confidence interval, the Company\' foreign exchange portfolio due adverse movements rates. The VAR model not intended represent actual losses but used risk estimation and management tool. The model assumes normal market conditions. Forecasted transactions, firm commitments, and assets and liabilities denominated foreign currencies were excluded from the model. Based the results the model, the Company estimates with % confidence maximum one-day loss fair value $ million September , compared maximum one-day loss $ million September , . Because the Company uses foreign currency instruments for hedging purposes, losses incurred those instruments are generally offset increases the fair value the underlying exposures. Actual gains and losses the future associated with the Company\' investment portfolio and derivative positions may differ materially from the sensitivity analyses performed September , due the inherent limitations associated with predicting the changes the timing and amount interest rates, foreign currency exchanges rates, and the Company\' actual exposures and positions. The Company also designs, develops and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music and audio books. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force and third-party wholesalers, resellers and value added resellers. addition its own hardware, software and peripheral products, the Company sells variety third-party hardware and software products through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business and government customers. Basis Presentation and Preparation The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts the Company. Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. The preparation these consolidated financial statements conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles requires management make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported these consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior year amounts the consolidated financial statements and notes thereto have been reclassified conform the current year presentation. Typically, the Company\' fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Fiscal years , and were each -week years. However, approximately every six years, the Company reports -week fiscal year align its fiscal quarters with calendar quarters adding week its first fiscal quarter. The Company expects add this additional week its first fiscal quarter . All information presented herein based the Company\' fiscal calendar. Financial Instruments Cash Equivalents and Short-term Investments All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less the date purchase are classified cash equivalents. Highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. Management determines the appropriate classification its investments debt and marketable equity securities the time purchase and reevaluates such designation each balance sheet date. The Company\' debt and marketable equity securities have been classified and accounted for available-for-sale. These securities are carried fair value, with the unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported component shareholders\' equity. The cost securities sold based upon the specific identification method. SFAS . requires issuers classify liabilities ( assets some circumstances) certain freestanding financial instruments that embody obligations for the issuer and have characteristics both liabilities and equity. The Company adopted the provisions SFAS . June , , which resulted favorable cumulative-effect type adjustment approximately $ million. The net gain loss the effective portion derivative instrument that designated economic hedge the foreign currency translation exposure the net investment foreign operation reported the same manner foreign currency translation adjustment. Changes the expected future cash flows the forecasted hedged transaction and changes the fair value the forward hedge are both measured from the contract rate the forward exchange rate associated with the forward contract\' maturity date. Foreign Currency Translation The Company translates the assets and liabilities its international non- . functional currency subsidiaries into . dollars using exchange rates effect the end each period. Revenue and expenses for these subsidiaries are translated using rates that approximate those effect during the period. Gains and losses from these translations are credited charged foreign currency translation included "accumulated other comprehensive income (loss)" shareholders\' equity. The Company\' foreign manufacturing subsidiaries and certain other international subsidiaries that use the . dollar their functional currency remeasure monetary assets and liabilities exchange rates effect the end each period, and inventories, property, and nonmonetary assets and liabilities historical rates. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products (hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Revenue from extended warranty and support contracts deferred and recognized ratably over the warranty and support periods. These contracts typically include extended phone support, certain repairs, web-based support resources, diagnostic tools, and extend the Company\' one-year basic limited parts and labor warranty. The Company sells software and peripheral products obtained from other companies. The Company establishes its own pricing and retains related inventory risk, the primary obligor sales transactions with its customers, and assumes the credit risk for amounts billed its customers. Accordingly, the Company recognizes revenue for the sale products obtained from other companies the gross amount billed. Revenue arrangements that include multiple elements such hardware, software, and services allocated each element based the relative fair value each element, which generally determined vendor specific objective evidence (VSOE). Allocated revenue for each element recognized when revenue recognition criteria have been met for each element. VSOE determined based the price charged when each element sold separately. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Generally, the Company does not offer specified unspecified upgrade rights its customers connection with software sales the sale extended warranty and support contracts. However, limited number the Company\' software products are available with maintenance agreements that grant customers rights unspecified future upgrades over the maintenance term when and available basis. Revenue associated with such maintenance recognized ratably over the maintenance term. Therefore, costs incurred subsequent achievement technological feasibility are usually not significant, and generally all software development costs have been expensed. Restructuring Charges June , the FASB issued SFAS . , Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit Disposal Activities . SFAS . supersedes Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) Issue . - , Liability Recognition for Certain Employee Termination Benefits and Other Costs Exit Activity (Including Certain Costs Associated with Restructuring) and requires that liability for cost associated with exit disposal activity recognized when the liability incurred, opposed when management commits exit plan. SFAS . also establishes that the liability should initially measured and recorded fair value. This Statement was effective for exit disposal activities initiated after December , . The provisions SFAS . were required applied prospectively after the adoption date newly initiated exit activities. Stock-Based Compensation The Company measures compensation expense for its employee stock-based compensation plans using the intrinsic value method prescribed Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion . , Accounting for Stock Issued Employees. The Company applies the disclosure provisions SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation , amended SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation\x97Transition and Disclosure the fair value-based method had been applied measuring compensation expense. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, discussed below, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. required under SFAS . , the pro forma effects stock-based compensation net income and earnings per common share for employee stock options granted and employee stock purchase plan share purchases have been estimated the date grant and beginning the period, respectively, using Black-Scholes option pricing model. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income (loss) over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. The Black-Scholes option valuation model was developed for use estimating the fair value freely traded options that have vesting restrictions and are fully transferable. addition, option valuation models require the input highly subjective assumptions including the expected life options and the Company\' expected stock price volatility. Because the Company\' employee stock options and employee ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK027:[04PAL0 04PAL1620]EA1620A.; \',USER=\'DNICHOL\', =\'; -DEC- ; : \' stock purchase plan shares have characteristics significantly different from those freely traded options, and because changes the subjective input assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate, management\' opinion, the existing models not provide reliable measure the fair value the Company\' employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income (loss) over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. Comprehensive Income Comprehensive income consists two components, net income and other comprehensive income. Other comprehensive income refers revenue, expenses, gains and losses that under generally accepted accounting principles are recorded element shareholders\' equity but are excluded from net income. The Company\' other comprehensive income comprised foreign currency translation adjustments from those subsidiaries not using the . dollar their functional currency, unrealized gains and losses marketable securities categorized available-for-sale, and net deferred gains and losses certain derivative instruments accounted for cash flow hedges. Foreign Exchange Risk Management The Company may enter into foreign currency forward and option contracts with financial institutions protect against foreign exchange risk associated with existing assets and liabilities, certain firmly committed transactions and forecasted future cash flows. Generally, the Company\' practice hedge majority its existing material foreign exchange transaction exposures. However, the Company may not hedge certain foreign exchange transaction exposures due immateriality, prohibitive economic cost hedging particular exposures, limited availability appropriate hedging instruments. protect gross margins from fluctuations foreign currency exchange rates, the Company\' . dollar functional subsidiaries hedge portion forecasted foreign currency revenues, and the Company\' non- . dollar functional subsidiaries selling local currencies hedge portion forecasted inventory purchases not denominated the subsidiaries\' functional currency. Other comprehensive income associated with hedges foreign currency revenues recognized component net sales the same period the related sales are recognized, and other comprehensive income related inventory purchases recognized component cost sales the same period the related costs are recognized. Typically, the Company hedges portions its forecasted foreign currency exposure associated with revenues and inventory purchases over time horizon months. Derivative instruments designated cash flow hedges must dedesignated hedges when probable that the forecasted hedged transaction will not occur the initially identified time period within subsequent month time period. Deferred gains and losses other comprehensive income associated with such derivative instruments are immediately reclassified into earnings other income and expense. Any subsequent changes fair value such derivative instruments are also reflected current earnings unless they are redesignated hedges other transactions. Interest Rate Risk Management From time time, the Company historically entered into interest rate derivative transactions with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income its cash equivalents and short-term investments with its fixed-rate interest expense any outstanding long-term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short-term . interest rates. prior years, the Company had entered into interest rate debt swaps with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income cash equivalents and short term investments with its fixed rate interest expense its long term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short term . interest rates. The interest rate swaps required the Company pay floating interest rate based the three- six-month . dollar LIBOR and receive fixed rate interest without exchanges the underlying notional amounts. These swaps effectively converted the Company\' fixed-rate -year debt floating-rate debt. Due prevailing market interest rates, during and the Company entered into and then subsequently closed out interest rate debt swap positions realizing gains $ million which were deferred over the remaining life the debt. Contingencies Beginning September , , three shareholder class action lawsuits were filed the . District Court for the Northern District California against the Company and its Chief Executive Officer. These lawsuits are substantially identical, and purport bring suit behalf persons who purchased the Company\' publicly traded common stock between July , , and September , . The complaints allege violations the Securities Exchange Act and seek unspecified compensatory damages and other relief. The Company believes these claims are without merit and intends defend them vigorously. The Company filed motion dismiss June , , which was heard the Court September , . December , , the Court granted the Company\' motion dismiss for failure state cause action, with leave Plaintiffs amend their complaint within thirty days. Plaintiffs filed their amended complaint January , , and March , , the Company filed motion dismiss the amended complaint. The Court heard the Company\' motion July , and dismissed Plaintiffs\' claims with prejudice August , . Plaintiffs have appealed the ruling. The Company subject certain other legal proceedings and claims that have arisen the ordinary course business and have not been fully adjudicated. the opinion management, the Company does not have potential liability related any current legal proceedings and claims that would individually the aggregate have material adverse effect its financial condition, liquidity results operations. However, the results legal proceedings cannot predicted with certainty. Should the Company fail prevail any these legal matters should several these legal matters resolved against the Company the same reporting period, the operating results particular reporting period could materially adversely affected. Note \x97Segment Information and Geographic Data accordance with SFAS . , Disclosures about Segments Enterprise and Related Information , the Company reports segment information based the "management" approach. The management approach designates the internal reporting used management for making decisions and assessing performance the source the Company\' reportable segments. The Company manages its business primarily geographic basis. The Company\' reportable operating segments are comprised the Americas, Europe, Japan, and Retail. The Americas segment includes both North and South America, except for the activities the Company\' Retail segment. The Europe segment includes European countries well the Middle East and Africa. The Japan segment includes only Japan and excludes revenue from the Company\' own retail stores Japan, which included the Company\' Retail segment. The Retail segment operated Apple-owned retail stores the . and Japan during fiscal . Other operating segments include Asia-Pacific, which includes Australia and Asia except for Japan, and the Company\' subsidiary, FileMaker, Inc. Each reportable geographic operating segment provides similar hardware and software products and similar services, and the accounting policies the various segments are the same those described Note , "Summary Significant Accounting Policies," except described below for the Retail segment. The Company evaluates the performance its operating segments based net sales. The Retail segment\' performance also evaluated based operating income. Net sales for geographic segments are generally based the location the customers. Operating income for each segment includes net sales third parties, related cost sales, and operating expenses directly attributable the segment. Operating income for each segment excludes other income and expense and certain expenses that are managed outside the operating segments. Costs excluded from segment operating income include various corporate expenses, manufacturing costs not included standard costs, income taxes, and various nonrecurring charges. Corporate expenses include research and development, corporate marketing expenses, and other separately managed general and administrative expenses including certain corporate expenses associated with support the Retail segment. The Company does not include intercompany transfers between segments for management reporting purposes. Segment assets exclude corporate assets. Corporate assets include cash, short-term and long-term investments, manufacturing facilities, miscellaneous corporate infrastructure, goodwill and other acquired intangible assets, and retail store construction- -progress that not subject depreciation. Except for the Retail segment, capital expenditures for long-lived assets are not reported management segment. Capital expenditures the Retail segment were $ million, $ million and $ million for , and , respectively. Operating income for all segments, except Retail, includes cost sales manufacturing standard cost, other cost sales, related sales and marketing costs, and certain general and administrative costs. This measure operating income, which includes manufacturing profit, provides comparable basis for comparison between the Company\' various geographic segments. Board Committees The Board has standing Compensation Committee, Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee (" Nominating Committee" ) and Audit and Finance Committee (" Audit Committee "). The Compensation Committee primarily responsible for reviewing the compensation arrangements for the Company\' executive officers, including the Chief Executive Officer, and for administering the Company\' stock option plans. Members the Compensation Committee are Messrs. Campbell, Drexler and Gore. The Nominating Committee assists the Board identifying qualified individuals become directors, determines the composition the Board and its committees, monitors the process assess Board effectiveness and helps develop and implement the Company\' corporate governance guidelines. Members the Nominating Committee are Messrs. Drexler and Gore and . Levinson. The Audit Committee primarily responsible for overseeing the services performed the Company\' independent auditors and internal audit department, evaluating the Company\' accounting policies and its system internal controls and reviewing significant financial transactions. Members the Audit Committee are Messrs. Campbell and York and . Levinson. The Audit, Compensation and Nominating Committees operate under written charters adopted the Board. These charters are available the Company\' website www apple com investor. Arrangements with Named Executive Officers Change Control Arrangements\x97Stock Options, Restricted Stock, and Restricted Stock Units the event "change control" the Company, all outstanding options under the Company\' stock option plans, except the Director Plan, will, unless otherwise determined the plan administrator, become exercisable full, and will cashed out amount equal the difference between the applicable "change control price" and the exercise price. The Director Plan provides that upon "change control" the Company, all unvested options held non-employee directors will automatically become fully vested and exercisable and will cashed out amount equal the difference between the applicable "change control price" and the exercise price the options. "change control" under these plans generally defined ( ) the acquisition any person % more the combined voting power the Company\' outstanding securities ( ) the occurrence transaction requiring shareholder approval and involving the sale all substantially all the assets the Company the merger the Company with into another corporation. addition, options, restricted stock grants, and restricted stock units granted the Named Executive Officers generally provide that the event there "change control," defined the Company\' stock option plans, and connection with following such "change control," their employment terminated without "Cause" they should resign for "Good Reason," those options, restricted stock, and restricted stock units outstanding that are not yet vested the date such "change control" shall become fully vested. Further, restricted stock and restricted stock units granted the Named Executive Officers also provide that, the event the Company terminates the Officer without cause any time, the restricted stock units and restricted stock will vest full. Generally, "Cause" defined include felony conviction, willful disclosure confidential information willful and continued failure perform his her employment duties. "Good Reason" includes resignation employment result substantial diminution position duties, adverse change title reduction annual base salary. Item . Policy Audit Committee Pre-Approval Audit and Non-Audit Services Performed the Independent Registered Public Accounting Firm Prior the enactment the Sarbanes-Oxley Act (the " Act "), the Company adopted auditor independence policy that banned its auditors from performing non-financial consulting services, such information technology consulting and internal audit services. This auditor policy also mandates that the audit and non-audit services and the related budget approved the Audit Committee advance, and that the Audit Committee provided with quarterly reporting actual spending. This policy also mandates that auditor engagements for non-audit services may entered into without the express approval the Audit Committee. Executive Overview Apple designs, manufactures and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops and markets line portable digital music ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK027:[04PAL0 04PAL1620]DI1620A.; \',USER=\'DNICHOL\', =\'; -DEC- ; : \' players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music and audio books. The Company\' products and services include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the iPod digital music player, the Xserve server and Xserve RAID storage products, portfolio consumer and professional software applications, the Mac operating system, the online iTunes Music Store, portfolio peripherals that support and enhance the Macintosh and iPod product lines, and variety other service and support offerings. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers and value added resellers. addition, the Company sells variety third-party Macintosh compatible products, including computer printers and printing supplies, storage devices, computer memory, digital video and still cameras, personal digital assistants, and various other computing products and supplies through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business and government customers. further description the Company\' products may found Part , Item this document under the heading "Business." The Company\' business strategy leverages its unique ability, through the design and development its own operating system, hardware and many software applications and technologies, bring its customers around the world compelling new products and solutions with superior ease- -use, seamless integration and innovative industrial design. The Company participates several highly competitive markets, including personal computers with its Macintosh line computers, consumer electronics with its iPod line digital music players and distribution third-party digital music through its online iTunes Music Store. While the Company widely recognized innovator the personal computer market well leader the emerging market for distribution digital music, these are highly competitive markets that are subject aggressive pricing and increased competition. order remain competitive, the Company believes that increased investment research and development ( & ) necessary order maintain and extend its position the markets where competes. The Company\' & spending focused delivering timely updates and enhancements its existing line personal computers, displays, operating systems, software applications and portable music players; developing new digital lifestyle consumer and professional software applications; and investing new product areas such rack-mount servers, RAID storage systems, and wireless technologies. The Company utilizes variety direct and indirect distribution channels. The Company believes that sales its innovative and differentiated products are enhanced knowledgeable salespersons who can convey the value the hardware, software and peripheral integration, demonstrate the unique digital lifestyle solutions that are available only Macintosh computers, and demonstrate the seamless compatibility the Macintosh with the Windows platform and networks. The Company further believes that providing high-quality sales and after-sales support experience critical attracting and retaining customers. ensure high-quality buying experience for its products which service and education are emphasized, the Company has expanded and improved its distribution capabilities opening its own retail stores the . and internationally. The Company had stores open September , . The Company has also staffed selected third-party stores with the Company\' own employees improve the buying experience through reseller channels. The Company also sells customers direct through one its online stores around the world. improve the accessibility its iPod product line, the Company has significantly expanded the number distribution points where iPods are sold. The iPod product line can now purchased department stores, discount stores and specialty music and audio-visual stores. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products ( ., hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition. The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped, and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end-user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Future market conditions and product transitions may require the Company increase customer incentive programs and incur incremental price protection obligations that could result additional reductions revenue the time such programs are offered. Additionally, certain customer incentive programs require management estimate the number customers who will actually redeem the incentive based historical experience and the specific terms and conditions particular incentive programs. greater than estimated proportion customers redeem such incentives, the Company would required record additional reductions revenue, which could have material adverse impact the Company\' results operations. Inventory Valuation and Inventory Purchase Commitments The Company must order components for its products and build inventory advance product shipments. The Company records write-down for inventories components and products, including third-party products held for resale, which have become obsolete are excess anticipated demand net realizable value. The Company performs detailed review inventory each period that considers multiple factors including demand forecasts, product life cycle status, product development plans, current sales levels, and component cost trends. The personal computer industry subject rapid and unpredictable pace product and component obsolescence and demand changes. future demand market conditions for the Company\' products are less favorable than forecasted unforeseen technological changes negatively impact the utility component inventory, the Company may required record additional write-downs which would negatively affect gross margins the period when the write-downs are recorded. The Company accrues necessary reserves for cancellation fees related component orders that have been cancelled. Consistent with industry practice, the Company acquires components through combination formal purchase orders, supplier contracts, and open orders based projected demand information. These commitments typically cover the Company\' requirements for periods ranging from days. there abrupt and substantial decline demand for one more the Company\' products unanticipated change technological requirements for any the Company\' products, the Company may required record additional reserves for cancellation fees that would negatively affect gross margins the period when the cancellation fees are identified. Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation The Company currently measures compensation expense for its employee stock-based compensation plans using the intrinsic value method prescribed Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion . , Accounting for Stock Issued Employees and provides pro forma disclosures the effect net income and earnings per share the fair value-based method had been applied measuring compensation expense. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, further discussed Part , Item this Form - Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation , requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. March , , the FASB issued proposed Statement, Share-Based Payment, that addresses the accounting for share-based payment transactions which enterprise receives employee services exchange for ( ) equity instruments the enterprise ( ) liabilities that are based the fair value the enterprise\' equity instruments that may settled the issuance such equity instruments. The proposed Statement would eliminate the ability account for share-based compensation transactions using APB Opinion . and generally would require instead that such transactions accounted for using fair-value-based method. adopted, currently anticipated that the proposed Statement would effective for the Company beginning its fourth fiscal quarter . the Company\' annual shareholders meeting April , , shareholders approved proposal requesting that the Company\' Board Directors (the Board) establish policy expensing the value all future employee stock options issued the Company. The Board and management appreciate and take seriously the views expressed the Company\' shareholders. The Company decided not expense the value employee stock options until the FASB finalizes its new accounting standard the matter, which may play significant role determining the fair value and accounting for employee stock options. The Company monitors progress the FASB and other developments with respect the general issue employee stock compensation. The Company currently reviewing the potential impact from the guidance the proposed statement, which may require the Company recognize substantially more compensation expense future periods that could have material adverse impact the Company\' future results operations. The accounting impact had the Company chosen apply the fair-value recognition provisions SFAS . , instead the recognition provisions under APB Opinion . , described Part , Item this Form - Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements. Purchase Obligations The Company utilizes several contract manufacturers manufacture sub-assemblies for the Company\' products and perform final assembly and test finished products. The Company also obtains individual components for its products from wide variety individual suppliers. The Company also designs, develops and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music and audio books. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force and third-party wholesalers, resellers and value added resellers. addition its own hardware, software and peripheral products, the Company sells variety third-party hardware and software products through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business and government customers. Basis Presentation and Preparation The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts the Company. Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. The preparation these consolidated financial statements conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles requires management make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported these consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior year amounts the consolidated financial statements and notes thereto have been reclassified conform the current year presentation. Typically, the Company\' fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Fiscal years , and were each -week years. However, approximately every six years, the Company reports -week fiscal year align its fiscal quarters with calendar quarters adding week its first fiscal quarter. The Company expects add this additional week its first fiscal quarter . All information presented herein based the Company\' fiscal calendar. Financial Instruments Cash Equivalents and Short-term Investments All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less the date purchase are classified cash equivalents. Highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. Management determines the appropriate classification its investments debt and marketable equity securities the time purchase and reevaluates such designation each balance sheet date. The Company\' debt and marketable equity securities have been classified and accounted for available-for-sale. These securities are carried fair value, with the unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported component shareholders\' equity. The cost securities sold based upon the specific identification method. Financial Instruments with Characteristics Both Liabilities and Equity May , , the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued Statement Financial Accounting Standards (SFAS) . , Accounting for Certain Financial Instruments with Characteristics Both Liabilities and Equity . SFAS . requires issuers classify liabilities ( assets some circumstances) certain freestanding financial instruments that embody obligations for the issuer and have characteristics both liabilities and equity. The Company adopted the provisions SFAS . June , , which resulted favorable cumulative-effect type adjustment approximately $ million. This adjustment related forward purchase agreement that allowed the Company acquire million shares its common stock average price $ per share for total cost $ million. Inventories Inventories are stated the lower cost (first- , first-out) market. the cost the inventories exceeds their market value, provisions are made currently for the difference between the cost and the market value. Foreign Currency Translation The Company translates the assets and liabilities its international non- . functional currency subsidiaries into . dollars using exchange rates effect the end each period. Revenue and expenses for these subsidiaries are translated using rates that approximate those effect during the period. Gains and losses from these translations are credited charged foreign currency translation included "accumulated other comprehensive income (loss)" shareholders\' equity. The Company\' foreign manufacturing subsidiaries and certain other international subsidiaries that use the . dollar their functional currency remeasure monetary assets and liabilities exchange rates effect the end each period, and inventories, property, and nonmonetary assets and liabilities historical rates. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products (hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Revenue from extended warranty and support contracts deferred and recognized ratably over the warranty and support periods. These contracts typically include extended phone support, certain repairs, web-based support resources, diagnostic tools, and extend the Company\' one-year basic limited parts and labor warranty. The Company sells software and peripheral products obtained from other companies. The Company establishes its own pricing and retains related inventory risk, the primary obligor sales transactions with its customers, and assumes the credit risk for amounts billed its customers. Accordingly, the Company recognizes revenue for the sale products obtained from other companies the gross amount billed. Revenue arrangements that include multiple elements such hardware, software, and services allocated each element based the relative fair value each element, which generally determined vendor specific objective evidence (VSOE). Allocated revenue for each element recognized when revenue recognition criteria have been met for each element. VSOE determined based the price charged when each element sold separately. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Generally, the Company does not offer specified unspecified upgrade rights its customers connection with software sales the sale extended warranty and support contracts. However, limited number the Company\' software products are available with maintenance agreements that grant customers rights unspecified future upgrades over the maintenance term when and available basis. Revenue associated with such maintenance recognized ratably over the maintenance term. Warranty Expense The Company provides currently for the estimated cost for product warranties the time the related revenue recognized. Research and Development Research and development costs are expensed incurred. Development costs computer software sold, leased otherwise marketed are subject capitalization beginning when product\' technological feasibility has been established and ending when product available for general release customers pursuant SFAS . , Computer Software Sold, Leased, Otherwise Marketed . most instances, the Company\' products are released soon after technological feasibility has been established. Therefore, costs incurred subsequent achievement technological feasibility are usually not significant, and generally all software development costs have been expensed. During the fourth quarter , the Company incurred substantial development costs associated with the development Mac version (code-named "Tiger"), which enhances the features and functionality the previous version Mac , subsequent achievement technological feasibility evidenced public demonstration August and subsequent release developer beta version the product, both which were prior the planned release the final version the product the first half calendar year . Therefore, during the fourth quarter , the Company capitalized approximately $ million costs associated with development Tiger. Amortization this asset will begin when Tiger begins shipping and will recognized straight-line over year estimated useful life. During the second quarter , the Company incurred substantial development costs associated with FileMaker Pro subsequent achievement technological feasibility evidenced public demonstration and release developer beta version, and prior the release the final version the product March . Restructuring Charges June , the FASB issued SFAS . , Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit Disposal Activities . SFAS . supersedes Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) Issue . - , Liability Recognition for Certain Employee Termination Benefits and Other Costs Exit Activity (Including Certain Costs Associated with Restructuring) and requires that liability for cost associated with exit disposal activity recognized when the liability incurred, opposed when management commits exit plan. SFAS . also establishes that the liability should initially measured and recorded fair value. This Statement was effective for exit disposal activities initiated after December , . The provisions SFAS . were required applied prospectively after the adoption date newly initiated exit activities. Stock-Based Compensation The Company measures compensation expense for its employee stock-based compensation plans using the intrinsic value method prescribed Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion . , Accounting for Stock Issued Employees. The Company applies the disclosure provisions SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation , amended SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation\x97Transition and Disclosure the fair value-based method had been applied measuring compensation expense. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, discussed below, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. required under SFAS . , the pro forma effects stock-based compensation net income and earnings per common share for employee stock options granted and employee stock purchase plan share purchases have been estimated the date grant and beginning the period, respectively, using Black-Scholes option pricing model. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income (loss) over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. The Black-Scholes option valuation model was developed for use estimating the fair value freely traded options that have vesting restrictions and are fully transferable. addition, option valuation models require the input highly subjective assumptions including the expected life options and the Company\' expected stock price volatility. Because the Company\' employee stock options and employee ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK027:[04PAL0 04PAL1620]EA1620A.; \',USER=\'DNICHOL\', =\'; -DEC- ; : \' stock purchase plan shares have characteristics significantly different from those freely traded options, and because changes the subjective input assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate, management\' opinion, the existing models not provide reliable measure the fair value the Company\' employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income (loss) over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. Comprehensive Income Comprehensive income consists two components, net income and other comprehensive income. Other comprehensive income refers revenue, expenses, gains and losses that under generally accepted accounting principles are recorded element shareholders\' equity but are excluded from net income. The Company\' other comprehensive income comprised foreign currency translation adjustments from those subsidiaries not using the . dollar their functional currency, unrealized gains and losses marketable securities categorized available-for-sale, and net deferred gains and losses certain derivative instruments accounted for cash flow hedges. Foreign Exchange Risk Management The Company may enter into foreign currency forward and option contracts with financial institutions protect against foreign exchange risk associated with existing assets and liabilities, certain firmly committed transactions and forecasted future cash flows. Generally, the Company\' practice hedge majority its existing material foreign exchange transaction exposures. However, the Company may not hedge certain foreign exchange transaction exposures due immateriality, prohibitive economic cost hedging particular exposures, limited availability appropriate hedging instruments. protect gross margins from fluctuations foreign currency exchange rates, the Company\' . dollar functional subsidiaries hedge portion forecasted foreign currency revenues, and the Company\' non- . dollar functional subsidiaries selling local currencies hedge portion forecasted inventory purchases not denominated the subsidiaries\' functional currency. Other comprehensive income associated with hedges foreign currency revenues recognized component net sales the same period the related sales are recognized, and other comprehensive income related inventory purchases recognized component cost sales the same period the related costs are recognized. Typically, the Company hedges portions its forecasted foreign currency exposure associated with revenues and inventory purchases over time horizon months. Derivative instruments designated cash flow hedges must dedesignated hedges when probable that the forecasted hedged transaction will not occur the initially identified time period within subsequent month time period. Deferred gains and losses other comprehensive income associated with such derivative instruments are immediately reclassified into earnings other income and expense. Any subsequent changes fair value such derivative instruments are also reflected current earnings unless they are redesignated hedges other transactions. Interest Rate Risk Management From time time, the Company historically entered into interest rate derivative transactions with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income its cash equivalents and short-term investments with its fixed-rate interest expense any outstanding long-term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short-term . interest rates. prior years, the Company had entered into interest rate debt swaps with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income cash equivalents and short term investments with its fixed rate interest expense its long term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short term . interest rates. The interest rate swaps required the Company pay floating interest rate based the three- six-month . dollar LIBOR and receive fixed rate interest without exchanges the underlying notional amounts. These swaps effectively converted the Company\' fixed-rate -year debt floating-rate debt. Due prevailing market interest rates, during and the Company entered into and then subsequently closed out interest rate debt swap positions realizing gains $ million which were deferred over the remaining life the debt. Contingencies Beginning September , , three shareholder class action lawsuits were filed the . District Court for the Northern District California against the Company and its Chief Executive Officer. These lawsuits are substantially identical, and purport bring suit behalf persons who purchased the Company\' publicly traded common stock between July , , and September , . The complaints allege violations the Securities Exchange Act and seek unspecified compensatory damages and other relief. The Company believes these claims are without merit and intends defend them vigorously. The Company filed motion dismiss June , , which was heard the Court September , . December , , the Court granted the Company\' motion dismiss for failure state cause action, with leave Plaintiffs amend their complaint within thirty days. Plaintiffs filed their amended complaint January , , and March , , the Company filed motion dismiss the amended complaint. The Court heard the Company\' motion July , and dismissed Plaintiffs\' claims with prejudice August , . Plaintiffs have appealed the ruling. The Company subject certain other legal proceedings and claims that have arisen the ordinary course business and have not been fully adjudicated. the opinion management, the Company does not have potential liability related any current legal proceedings and claims that would individually the aggregate have material adverse effect its financial condition, liquidity results operations. However, the results legal proceedings cannot predicted with certainty. Should the Company fail prevail any these legal matters should several these legal matters resolved against the Company the same reporting period, the operating results particular reporting period could materially adversely affected. Note \x97Segment Information and Geographic Data accordance with SFAS . , Disclosures about Segments Enterprise and Related Information , the Company reports segment information based the "management" approach. The management approach designates the internal reporting used management for making decisions and assessing performance the source the Company\' reportable segments. The Company manages its business primarily geographic basis. The Company\' reportable operating segments are comprised the Americas, Europe, Japan, and Retail. The Americas segment includes both North and South America, except for the activities the Company\' Retail segment. The Europe segment includes European countries well the Middle East and Africa. The Japan segment includes only Japan and excludes revenue from the Company\' own retail stores Japan, which included the Company\' Retail segment. The Retail segment operated Apple-owned retail stores the . and Japan during fiscal . Other operating segments include Asia-Pacific, which includes Australia and Asia except for Japan, and the Company\' subsidiary, FileMaker, Inc. Each reportable geographic operating segment provides similar hardware and software products and similar services, and the accounting policies the various segments are the same those described Note , "Summary Significant Accounting Policies," except described below for the Retail segment. The Company evaluates the performance its operating segments based net sales. The Retail segment\' performance also evaluated based operating income. Net sales for geographic segments are generally based the location the customers. Operating income for each segment includes net sales third parties, related cost sales, and operating expenses directly attributable the segment. Operating income for each segment excludes other income and expense and certain expenses that are managed outside the operating segments. Costs excluded from segment operating income include various corporate expenses, manufacturing costs not included standard costs, income taxes, and various nonrecurring charges. Corporate expenses include research and development, corporate marketing expenses, and other separately managed general and administrative expenses including certain corporate expenses associated with support the Retail segment. The Company does not include intercompany transfers between segments for management reporting purposes. Segment assets exclude corporate assets. Corporate assets include cash, short-term and long-term investments, manufacturing facilities, miscellaneous corporate infrastructure, goodwill and other acquired intangible assets, and retail store construction- -progress that not subject depreciation. Except for the Retail segment, capital expenditures for long-lived assets are not reported management segment. Capital expenditures the Retail segment were $ million, $ million and $ million for , and , respectively. Operating income for all segments, except Retail, includes cost sales manufacturing standard cost, other cost sales, related sales and marketing costs, and certain general and administrative costs. This measure operating income, which includes manufacturing profit, provides comparable basis for comparison between the Company\' various geographic segments. Role the Board; Corporate Governance Matters the paramount duty the Board Directors oversee the Chief Executive Officer and other senior management the competent and ethical operation the Company day- -day basis and assure that the long-term interests the shareholders are being served. satisfy this duty, the directors take proactive, focused approach their position, and set standards ensure that the Company committed business success through maintenance the highest standards responsibility and ethics. Members the Board bring the Company wide range experience, knowledge and judgment. These varied skills mean that good governance depends far more than "check the box" approach standards procedures. The governance structure the Company designed working structure for principled actions, effective decision-making and appropriate monitoring both compliance and performance. The key practices and procedures the Board are outlined the Corporate Governance Guidelines available the Company\' website www apple com investor. Board Committees The Board has standing Compensation Committee, Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee (" Nominating Committee" ) and Audit and Finance Committee (" Audit Committee "). The Compensation Committee primarily responsible for reviewing the compensation arrangements for the Company\' executive officers, including the Chief Executive Officer, and for administering the Company\' stock option plans. Members the Compensation Committee are Messrs. Campbell, Drexler and Gore. The Nominating Committee assists the Board identifying qualified individuals become directors, determines the composition the Board and its committees, monitors the process assess Board effectiveness and helps develop and implement the Company\' corporate governance guidelines. Members the Nominating Committee are Messrs. Drexler and Gore and . Levinson. The Audit Committee primarily responsible for overseeing the services performed the Company\' independent auditors and internal audit department, evaluating the Company\' accounting policies and its system internal controls and reviewing significant financial transactions. Members the Audit Committee are Messrs. Campbell and York and . Levinson. The Audit, Compensation and Nominating Committees operate under written charters adopted the Board. These charters are available the Company\' website www apple com investor.
